    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText12833634034557634235" style="display:none">No one expects a princess to be brutal. And Lada Dragwlya likes it that way. Ever since she and her gentle younger brother, Radu, were wrenched from their homeland of Wallachia and abandoned by their father to be raised in the Ottoman courts, Lada has known that being ruthless is the key to survival. She and Radu are doomed to act as pawns in a vicious game, an unseen sword hovering over their every move. For the lineage that makes them special also makes them targets.<br /><br />Lada despises the Ottomans and bides her time, planning her vengeance for the day when she can return to Wallachia and claim her birthright. Radu longs only for a place where he feels safe. And when they meet Mehmed, the defiant and lonely son of the sultan, Radu feels that he’s made a true friend—and Lada wonders if she’s finally found someone worthy of her passion.<br /><br />But Mehmed is heir to the very empire that Lada has sworn to fight against—and that Radu now considers home. Together, Lada, Radu, and Mehmed form a toxic triangle that strains the bonds of love and loyalty to the breaking point.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/702727-why-is-this-book-labelled-as">Why is this book labelled as 

Fantasy
Fantasy &gt; Dragons
Fantasy &gt; High Fantasy
Young Adult &gt; Young Adult Fantasy

there is not a single dragon, no magic, not magical beings. It&#39;s a reimagined historical story. It takes place in real parts of the world. It shouldn&#39;t be labelled as fantasy of any kind. Perhaps fantastical elements will enter the sequels but as of now it shouldn&#39;t have those labels. Why?</a>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/801183-does-it-contain-mentions-of-a-religion-in">does it contain mentions of a religion in anyway? (since we are talking about the Ottoman empire)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_801183'><a id="like_count_community_question_801183" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/801183?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F27190613-and-i-darken">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/17682216-brenda"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1494249471i/17682216._UX100_CR0,24,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/17682216-brenda">Brenda</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think that this book did a really good job at presenting religion in an unbiased way. That being said, depending on the CHARACTER that is describing<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think that this book did a really good job at presenting religion in an unbiased way. That being said, depending on the CHARACTER that is describing/experiencing the religion, it can be biased in how that character thinks of the religion. But the story itself takes a very unbiased historical view on all of it. It explains what roles the religions play in different situations, but doesn't focus on one being "better" than another.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1167268114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167268114" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167268114?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167268114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12639154256731996982"><blockquote>
  <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. <b>This book is totally fucked up</b>. In the best possible way.<br/><br/>Well, holy shit. Even with the positive reviews rolling in, that was completely unexpected. How do I begin to explain this vicious little nightmare of a book? All I know is: it's different to anything else I've read.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25324111.And_I_Darken__Conqueror_s_Saga___1_' title='And I Darken (Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'>And I Darken</a> is dark, gritty and compelling. It pulled me into its da</span>
  <span id="freeText12639154256731996982" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. <b>This book is totally fucked up</b>. In the best possible way.<br /><br />Well, holy shit. Even with the positive reviews rolling in, that was completely unexpected. How do I begin to explain this vicious little nightmare of a book? All I know is: it's different to anything else I've read.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25324111.And_I_Darken__Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> is dark, gritty and compelling. It pulled me into its darkness from the very first chapter and I didn't come up for air until I'd finished all 496 pages of it. It's the kind of book that is everything that hooks you, fuelling your rage and your desperate need to turn the page, whilst also being a <b>well-written, highly-original story</b>.<br /><br />"Fantasy" is a loose term for this book. You won't find any <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>-esque heroines or magic here. It's more alternate history, set in Transylvania at the height of the Ottoman Empire (based on history, though not historically accurate), and richer, more political than typical YA fantasy. <b>And much nastier</b>. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>As the baby latched on with surprising fierceness, the nurse offered her own prayer.<br />Let her be strong.<br />Let her be sly.<br />And let her be ugly.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Lada is a freaking fantastic, psychotic heroine</b>. She is not one of those faux-antiheroines who proclaim their badassery and never do anything other than defeat the bad guys and fall in love. From the moment she is born, she is fierce, resilient and a little bit nuts. As she grows, she becomes ever more cold, cruel and calculating. She quickly recognizes what it means to be a woman in this world and <b>she is not playing along</b>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“On our wedding night,” she said, “I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied.”</i>
</blockquote><br />In fact, she's furious. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25324111.And_I_Darken__Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> explores Lada's disdain for women and her own confused feelings over whether she should deny or defend her femininity. But don't worry, this is paired with the revelation that there are many kinds of power and women have their own ways of wielding it, biding their time and eventually getting what they want.<br /><br />However, though she is fascinating, the book isn't just about Lada. The third person narrative is also about the experiences of her brother - Radu, a beautiful, delicate boy whose weakness both aggravates Lada and draws her protection. They have a complex sibling relationship, once again quite unlike anything we usually see in YA, and it is filled with frustration, jealousy and misunderstanding.<br /><br />A few other things: <br />1) I absolutely loved this unconventional setting in Eastern Europe. It's so rare to see novels set here and I thought the author captured it perfectly. <br />2) I liked how the novel explored different religions and a lack of religion in a way that wasn't preachy - also very refreshing to see a non-judgmental portrayal of Islam. <br />3) There is <b>no love triangle</b>. There is a complex web of relationships that is guaranteed to get messy, but it is not a love triangle (at least not yet). I thought you might want to know because there are some LT signs early on.<br /><br />I loved this book. I really did. It's a gory, horrible trek into a place inspired by gory, historical truth. Everything is intricately-woven in perfect detail, from the setting to the characters, and from the relationships to the politics. It is <b>unlike anything Kiersten White has written before</b>. And it is virtually unputdownable. <br /><br />It's about power, and all the ways it can be gained and used. It's about women, and what it means to be a woman. And it's about fighting, every day, to be what you want.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The sooner you stop fighting, the easier your life will be. This is what your purpose is.”<br />Lada stood so abruptly she nearly fell backward. “No.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12639154256731996982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1686172311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686172311" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686172311?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=plotting">plotting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686172311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13854503051467161282"><blockquote>
  <em>‘‘The price of living seems to always be death.’’</em>
  <br/>
  <em>‘‘And that is why you become a dealer of death. You feed death as many people as you can to keep it full and content so its eye stays off you.’’</em>
</blockquote><br/><em>And I Darken </em>is no bedtime story. Its complexity makes it hard to get into but also hard to get out of.<br/><br/>I don’t know exactly when it happened, but sometime as I was reading it, I suddenly stopped thinking of it as <em>just another historical fiction/fantasy</em> story and started seeing it in a new light.<br/><br/>S</span>
  <span id="freeText13854503051467161282" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>‘‘The price of living seems to always be death.’’</em>
  <br />
  <em>‘‘And that is why you become a dealer of death. You feed death as many people as you can to keep it full and content so its eye stays off you.’’</em>
</blockquote><br /><em>And I Darken </em>is no bedtime story. Its complexity makes it hard to get into but also hard to get out of.<br /><br />I don’t know exactly when it happened, but sometime as I was reading it, I suddenly stopped thinking of it as <em>just another historical fiction/fantasy</em> story and started seeing it in a new light.<br /><br />Seeing it as a story of survival.<br /><br />Lada and Radu were supposed to die. They were forsaken by their own father, to assure the latter’s continuous reign. They were betrayed and now they have only each other to rely on.<br /><br />Lada is the strongest of the two but Radu is the charming one. As different as they may be, together, they are unstoppable.<br /><br /><em>And I Darken</em> steers clear of sugar-coating, and has a propensity for scheming and deceiving. Many revelations take time to appear, and perhaps that is why it is only after they started sprouting out that I became fully invested in it.<br /><br />Though I couldn’t help but <em>want to know more</em> and be interested in Lada and Radu’s fates from the first page. <br /><br />And I deeply felt for Radu when he started realizing the truth about himself.<br /><br />I must admit that the addition of a gay character was completely unexpected but I welcomed him and the theme that came with him with open arms.<br /><br />Do not expect for <em>And I Darken</em> to entertain you. It was not written to make anyone laugh or arise derision. It’s as <em>serious</em> as they get. I swear Lada and Radu will behold their first gray hair at the age of twenty.<br /><br />Everything they go through… Everything they experience… All the hopes that fall flat… All the dreams that are shattered… It all contributes to their (outstanding) character development.<br /><br />Their precarious future is the most interesting part. No one knows what will happen next (the book is full of surprises) and there is no indication of assured safety. They are on a tightrope—they always were.<br /><br />But one thing’s for sure. Mehmed must die. (Though this is simply a request, not a spoiler or anything I foresee.) Please kill him, Kiersten White. I hate his guts. Thank you.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13854503051467161282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2424391783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2424391783" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424391783?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424391783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8923218563412592247"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1606232004i/30422803._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567358690i/28084862._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>Rivetingly dark and heartbreakingly human. </b> <blockquote>
  <i> the nurse offered her own prayer.<br/><blockquote>Let her be strong.<br/>Let her be sly.<br/>And let her be ugly.</blockquote></i>
</blockquote> Much like the nurse's prayer, Lada Dragwlya grew up <b>single-minded, cruel and absolutely ruthless</b>. Completely in contrast to her beautiful younger brother, Radu.<blockquote>
  <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8923218563412592247" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1606232004i/30422803._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567358690i/28084862._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>Rivetingly dark and heartbreakingly human. </b> <blockquote>
  <i> the nurse offered her own prayer.<br><blockquote>Let her be strong.<br>Let her be sly.<br>And let her be ugly.</blockquote></i>
</blockquote> Much like the nurse's prayer, Lada Dragwlya grew up <b>single-minded, cruel and absolutely ruthless</b>. Completely in contrast to her beautiful younger brother, Radu.<blockquote>
  <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
</blockquote>Lada, and Radu, started life<b> almost entirely isolated. </b>They were occasionally visited by their warlord of a father and were raised by their nurse.<br><br>Soon, the siblings were taken from her homeland (Wallachia) at a young age to act as leverage against their father.<br><br> Lada decides then and there that she will come back to her people and her country and rule them with the <b>strength and brutal efficiency </b>that her father lacked. <blockquote>
  <i>Her spine was steel. Her heart was armor. Her eyes were fire.</i>
</blockquote> But until that day comes, Lada and Radu must navigate the intricacies of the Ottoman Empire - one wrong move could very well mean <b>the end of both their lives. </b><br><br>Wow. Seriously, wow. I love a <b>good, dark antihero book</b> and Lada absolutely delivered.<br><br>The way she <b>coldly and efficiently </b>denied the common expectations of the times just blew me away - take her response to a marriage proposal (well, more like she was commanded to marry).<blockquote>
  <i>“On our wedding night," she said, "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself.” </i>
</blockquote>And yet, she never became a caricature of a "strong-independent-woman." Lada had moments of weakness, self-pity and childhood doubt which kept character real in my eyes.<br><br>Radu was such a <b>precious child </b>- he never could handle the cruel world that Lada reveled in. His purity and love for Lada and Mehmed (the third son of the Ottoman emperor) provided an excellent backdrop that kept this book from feeling too harsh.<br><br>I absolutely loved the ending and cannot get my hands on book 2 fast enough.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Well-read by Fiona Hardingham - she had excellent pacing and tone. Thank goodness I listened to this one - there's quite a few words that I would definitely have pronounced wrong if I had only read them. (i.e. Wallachia is Val-heh-ahh).<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1235759623" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4843819376110179491"><b>4.5 stars</b> I didn't believe all the high ratings, and now here I am with them.<br/><br/>A good example of why it's good to try authors again, btw. I'd read a couple of the author's earlier books and found them likable if a bit unmemorable, but there was absolutely no indication that one day she'd write a brutal book--or an uncompromising heroine--like this. <br/><br/>Vlad the Impaler re-imagined as an aggressive girl! Fantastic. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1066104327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1066104327" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066104327?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552573740" href="/book/show/25324111-and-i-darken">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066104327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18281969166107916053">This was truly an epic book. There is a twist in this book, and trust me when I say that you will not see it coming.<br/><br/>It has a heroine who flaunts herself as the "anti-princess" and in that sense, the book does not disappoint. Lada - our "female Vlad the Impaler" hooked (impaled?) me from the start. Even as a child in the nursery, she was fierce.<blockquote>
  <i>Like her brother, Lada had big eyes, but hers were close-set, with arched bows that made her look perpetually cross. Her hair was a tangled mass, so da</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18281969166107916053" style="display:none">This was truly an epic book. There is a twist in this book, and trust me when I say that you will not see it coming.<br /><br />It has a heroine who flaunts herself as the "anti-princess" and in that sense, the book does not disappoint. Lada - our "female Vlad the Impaler" hooked (impaled?) me from the start. Even as a child in the nursery, she was fierce.<blockquote>
  <i>Like her brother, Lada had big eyes, but hers were close-set, with arched bows that made her look perpetually cross. Her hair was a tangled mass, so dark that her pale skin appeared sickly. Her nose was long and hooked, her lips thin, her teeth small and...quite sharp.<br /><br />She was contrary and vicious and the meanest child the nurse had ever cared for...In Lada she saw a spark, a passionate, fierce glimmer that refused to hide or be dimmed.</i>
</blockquote>I love anti-heroes, and Lada is as bad-ass as they come. This book is unusual because so rarely in YA fiction one gets a female character who is <b>absolutely brutal</b>. <br /><br /><b>Lada</b> is the daughter of Vlad Dracul. Upon her birth, she was dismissed. Warlords have no use for a daughter, girls being only useful if they're pretty enough to be married off. But surprisingly, as Lada grew, Vlad discovered in his daughter the strength and fierceness he himself admired, the qualities in a leader that was completely missing in his son Radu. <br /><br /><b>Radu</b> is a year younger than Lada, with all the beauty and grace and gentleness Lada lacks. To Vlad, Radu is, frankly, useless.<blockquote>
  <i>He embarrased no one. He remained unnoticed and invisible.<br /><br />It was, apparently, both the least and the most he could do for his father.</i>
</blockquote>This is the tale of two unwanted children, abandoned and left to fight for their survival in an Ottoman court. It's the story of a girl constrained by her gender, in a time where daughters are little more than chattel, and a young man trying to come out from his sister's shadow.<br /><br />I like Lada. I feel like she's a little bit <i>too much</i> in her fierceness sometimes. This book compares itself to <i>Game of Thrones</i>. I don't see the comparison at all, but I feel like if I had to pick a character, <b>Lada would be most like Brienne of Tarth</b>. Both are bred for battle, both deny and despise their feminity, both are unattractive, and at times, too severe, trying too hard to deny their emotions. Not the worst thing in the world, considering the number of swoony stupid female heroines out there, but at the same time, a little softness never hurts, a little gentleness would make Lada a more well-wounded character.<br /><br />She scratched and clawed her way into the world. Since she was a child, she literally fights for everything she has. She is aggressive, angry, short-tempered, intensely intelligent. <b>Her fury is palpable</b>, and she is so angry about so many things. She wants so many things. There is such a hunger in her for life and for what is hers. <br /><br />I really loved the brother-sister relationship between Radu and Lada. Love and hate is such a fine line. She is more or less his protector, in a stereotypical sense, she has the more masculine spirit, she is a warrior, and he is a poet. Their relationship is very complex, with Radu constantly seeking her approval, feeling (and often being told) that he is inferior to his fierce, strong older sister. An older sister who feels like he is her property.<blockquote>
  <i>She sat beside his bed for a long while. Finally, she put a hand on his shoulder and whispered, "You are mine."</i>
</blockquote>Like her brother, she seeks affirmation. Whereas Radu wants his sister be proud of him, Lada wants her father's approval.<br /><br />The setting is interesting and well-built. It's history-based, and honestly, I don't know much about the history of the region, but it feels authentic enough! It explores religions like Christianity and Islam (so rare!) without being preachy, only informative.<br /><br />The romance was not overwhelming, the relationship between Lada and Mehmed was build upon mutual dependency and trust, and not pure blind love and adoration. People are trying to kill them. They have to depend on each other. <b>Lada is no weakling, and Mehmed respects her for who she is.</b><br /><br />One of my favorite moments in the book was when Lada had a moment with a lady of the Ottoman court. She learned that there are more subtle ways to wage battle, that women can wield power through means other than fistfights, that everything has a price.<blockquote>
  <i>"You see this...as a prison. But you are wrong. This is my court. This is my throne. This is my kingdom. The cost was my freedom and my body...So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let me taken away so that you, too, can have power?"</i>
</blockquote>Overall, this was an <b>intensely satisfying, well-woven tale.</b><br /><br /><i>All quotes were taken from an advanced edition subject to change in the final edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18281969166107916053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1708420660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1708420660" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1708420660?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1708420660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14649041720376517196"><b>$1.99 on kindle right now! 6-26-17. As far as I know, it's US pricing</b> <br/><br/><b>Re-Read 2017</b> I had to read this book again for the new book next week. I love it so freaking much! This time I listened to it on audio from Overdrive (It's now on my audible wishlist) The narrator, Fiona Hardingham did a wonderful job! <br/><br/>It was so nice to be back in Lada's world. She's just so tough but I did feel sorry for her with the love interest but it's extremely complicated. She lets her guard down a little in that area b</span>
  <span id="freeText14649041720376517196" style="display:none"><b>$1.99 on kindle right now! 6-26-17. As far as I know, it's US pricing</b> <br><br><b>Re-Read 2017</b> I had to read this book again for the new book next week. I love it so freaking much! This time I listened to it on audio from Overdrive (It's now on my audible wishlist) The narrator, Fiona Hardingham did a wonderful job! <br><br>It was so nice to be back in Lada's world. She's just so tough but I did feel sorry for her with the love interest but it's extremely complicated. She lets her guard down a little in that area but she's still a force. Heh! That guy that tried to rape her, that didn't go as planned! I love it =]. Anyway, you can see my old review for excerpts and fun stuff =]<br><br>****Older Review****<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469672010i/19843161._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>Vlad Dracul's heavy brow descended like a storm when the doctor informed him that his wife had given birth to a girl.</b>
</i><br><br>Oh, little did he know that he would have one of the most brutal, bad@ssed girl known to man! <br><br><i>
  <b>Lada waved the knife at him in answer to the question she did not understand. Vlad raised an eyebrow. He was wrapped in a fine cloak, an elaborate hat on his head. It had been nearly a year since Lada had seen her father. She did not recognize him. <br><br>"Lada!" the nurse whispered. "Come here at once."<br><br>Lada stood as tall as her short, stocky legs allowed. "This is my home! I am the Order of the Dragon! I kill infidels!"</b>
</i><br><br>I am totally in love with the character of Ladislav Dragwlya (Lada). She is beyond bad. She just doesn't care and she will attack anyone. She wants to be equal with men. She doesn't care to be married off. She doesn't care to do women stuff. She trains to be a soldier, a warrior woman. She bad to the bone from the get go. <br><br><i>
  <b>Radu had braced for another blow when Aron's shout made him open his eyes. Aron was spinning in a circle, trying desperately to dislodge Lada. She was not supposed to be here, but somehow her presence was unsurprising. She had jumped on the boy's back, clasping her arms around him and pinning his arms to his sides. Radu could not see her face through her tangled drape of hair until Aron twisted to the side, revealing Lada's teeth sunk into his shoulder</b>
</i><br><br>I wish I could have been like her with all of the bullies in school :-) <br><br>Radu is Lada's younger brother, but she doesn't coddle him or give him comfort like a normal sister. She will take up for him but she will smack him around as well. Although, when they get a little older she's not as bad to him. <br><br>I was thinking this was going to be a cool book about the awesome Vlad and his kids but Vlad is like a little sissy compared to his daughter Lada. They sort of switched places. <br><br>This book took a lot of time building up to what I'm hoping is going to be an awesome saga. With that ending I do believe so. <br><br>Vlad let Halil Pasha take Lada and Radu to the Ottoman Court. He turned them over to an enemy. Although, he wasn't bad to the kids. He gave them schooling and decided to marry Lada off when the time came. Oh and that decision went down well, so she got sent off to another place with one of the sultan's sons to do more schooling with the son, Mehmed and her brother Radu. <br><br><i>
  <b>Lada spoke with a quiet, clear voice, and the room hushed in surprise. No one expected the girl to speak. She was probably not allowed to. Radu knew Lada would not care either way. "On our wedding night," she said. "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469672010ra/19843162.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is no one like her. To be that brutal and not take no sh*t in those times is just beyond coolness! <br><br>Lada eventually started training with the Janissaries. They are a form of soldiers that are paid a good wage. She became friends with them when she didn't take crap from them either. She eventually got her wish of becoming one of them, but oh so much more. <br><br><i>
  <b>"Not very pretty for a whore." The soldier behind her tugged on a strand of her hair. She ducked under his arm, grabbing his wrist and twisting it behind his back to pin him. It was a trick she learned under the harsh tutelage of Mircea and perfected by practicing on Bogdan and Radu. The soldier shouted angrily and tried to pull away, so she twisted harder, pushing up against the joint. He yelped in pain.<br><br>"You are prettier than I." She put more pressure on his arm. "Perhaps you could offer yourself as whore instead."</b>
</i><br><br>She's amazing! <br><br>Lada, Mehmed and Radu bond, as much as Lada allows herself to bond. I really enjoyed all of that storyline. There are some love interests in the book but they don't really go too far with that because it's more about kicking arse and getting the story set up. <br><br><i>
  <b>Lada huffed, exasperated. "Very well. What exactly does a friend do?"<br>"I have never had one. I was hoping you would know."<br>"Then you are even stupider than you look. Radu is the one who makes friends. I am the one who makes people want to whip me." <br><br>"Good. In the spirit of friendship, I must tell you that I am bitterly jealous of the time you spend in the Janisssaries' company. I want you to stop training with them. <br>"And, in the spirit of friendship, I must tell you that I do not care in the slightest about your petty jealousies. I am late for my training." She hooked her foot behind Mehmed's ankle, then slammed her shoulder into his, tripping him and throwing him to the ground.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460669816i/18772974.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At some point Mehmed becomes sultan when his father just decides to retire. There is a whole other story line going on there too, but I don't want to give out spoilers on certain things. Lada does end up saving a bunch of lives and there are more wars and what not. <br><br>Either way, I loved this book. I love Lada and I look forward to the rest of the books! Please be good! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469672010i/19843163.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Not Dragwlya," she said. "Lada Dracul. I am not longer the daughter of the dragon." She lifted her chin, sights set on the horizon. "I am the dragon."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469672010ra/19843164.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/07/and-i-darken-by-kiersten-white.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1708420660">

<div id="review_1688433158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688433158" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688433158?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688433158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8064758407358054060"><b>REREAD:</b> Because when it comes to needing to read a sequel...do I remember the first book? HA. I know nothing, Jon Snow. But this is the kind of book <b>that really grew on me the more I thought about it.</b> Several things still bugged me with my reread, but truuuuly I love this story. <3 It is the finest of historical fiction and the characters have caught my heart.<br/><br/><b>This news just in:</b> Radu is the most kind and precious and beautiful cinnamon roll of ever and also totally a cunning Slytherin. I call it.</span>
  <span id="freeText8064758407358054060" style="display:none"><b>REREAD:</b> Because when it comes to needing to read a sequel...do I remember the first book? HA. I know nothing, Jon Snow. But this is the kind of book <b>that really grew on me the more I thought about it.</b> Several things still bugged me with my reread, but truuuuly I love this story. &lt;3 It is the finest of historical fiction and the characters have caught my heart.<br /><br /><b>This news just in:</b> Radu is the most kind and precious and beautiful cinnamon roll of ever and also totally a cunning Slytherin. I call it.<br /><br /><b>I really appreciated the world building more this time!</b> And the detail with the historical elements! I listened to an audio so that also helped me focus a lot more. I do think the ending was a teeny bit slow and Mehmed is so frustrating (he is just a spoiled prince tho) and I wish Radu would find someone better to love him as he truly deserves to be loved &lt;3 RADU NEEDS ALL THE LOVE. I also wonder if Lada is possibly asexual? I feel like she liked Mehmed because he treated her as a person, not an object, but I still don't feel like she had any sexual want for him?<br /><br /><b>OKAY I NEED THE SEQUEL BADLY.</b>I'm so ready for this. Bring on my dragon queen Lada and my slytherin rainbow Radu and hopefully the chance for them to rule the world. I'm just sayin'.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ORIGINALLY READ IN JULY 2016</u>
</b>:<br /><br />WELL. WHERE DO I EVEN BEGIN WITH MY MAMMOTH TEAPOT LOAD OF THOUGHTS??? Because I have <i>many</i>, my fiends. The trouble is <b>this book had an enormous load of potential with all the epic characters and much stabbing -- and yet???? It felt dry.</b> Although at the same time I appreciate how UNIQUE the story is and how amazing all the historical elements are. <br /><br /><b>So basically I am like so:</b><br /><br />Me: This was deadly boring.<br />Brain: But the characters were precious violent cinnamon rolls.<br />Me: But I napped.<br />Brain: But <i>gender-swapped</i> Vlad the Impaler.<br />Me: ...<br />Brain: RIGHT???<br />Me: OK SO TRUE. SO COOL.<br /><br /><i>(Myself and I have very stimulating conversations btw.)</i><br /><br />BUT ONWARDS SINCE I SHOULD PROBABLY REVIEW THIS BEAST TOO. Today I'm going to give you a list of <b>Things This Book Is About:</b> So you know what to expect when you read it! Because I'm sure it would appeal to a LOT of people. But I think you also need to know what you're in for because it ain't your average YA.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>7 THINGS YOU SHOULD KNOW ABOUT THIS BOOK:</u>
</b><br /><br />•<b>It is NOT fantasy.</b><br />Whoever is bopping around the internet saying "Ooh fantasy!" is WRONG and needs to sit down. This is historical fiction. Granted it is gender-swapped, but I don't call that fantasy! I call that a retelling. So it's a <i>sort of</i> historical fiction <i>retelling</i>. But there is <b>zero magic</b> okay? OKAY. I think this needs to be cleared up!!<br /><br /><b>• It is very very very political.</b><br />It almost reminded me of Game of Thrones in that respect? Because basically it is 90% about who is at war with who and who wants to stab and impale who (spoiler: EVERYONE WANTS TO STAB EVERYONE) and alliances and broken alliances and who gets the throne and yadda yadda ya. I mean <b>it was interesting</b> but at the same time <b>it was deathly confusing</b>. I napped. I did. Guilty as charged, Marge.<br /><br /><b>• Want a spoonful of history? HERE LET ME CRAM IT ALL DOWN YOUR THROAT INSTEAD.</b><br />Like this is definitely not a bad thing if you like historical facts. Except (A) not all the facts ARE historical (the author mentions this in her note at the end) so I don't know whether to run around spewing details about this era or not, which is a bummer. And (B) there was <u>too much</u>. It actually drowned the story at times because we were too busy being told all these DETAILS about all these PEOPLE GROUPS who hated each other. Like seriously, please summarise: EVERYONE DISTRUSTS EVERYONE AND THERE'S STABBING. &lt;-- Look I wrote the book in 6 words. <b>I fully admit that it was so plot driven at times that I just felt my brain switching off.</b><br /><br /><b>• But the characters were precious murderous darlings.</b><br />Often I read books where the book crows "this character is so bad!" and the character, like, sneezes on a puppy and doesn't apologise or whatever. YOU GET NONE OF THAT HERE. <b>Lada is downright CRUEL.</b> She stabs and bites and she's 100% feral and wild and omg, she's amazing. I loved her. She is the most violent thing I've read in a long time. (And, that saying, the book isn't actually written very graphically, so rest your wee hearts in peace.) But BOOYAH! Lada is not the only narrating character.<b> It's actually 50% Lada and 50% Radu.</b> I loved this because <b>Radu was probably my favourite thing ever.</b> He's the "weak" one. He spent his childhood being abused and neglected (chiefly by Lada) and yet they still have this really strong bond? They are the only ones who trust each other. I REALLY LOVED THEIR SIBLING DYNAMICS. I honestly put these 2 characters as some of my favourites of <i>ever</i>. Which is why it pains me that the PLOT WAS SO DAMN BORING. <br /><br /><b> • Romance? We gotcha romance.</b><br />It is a love triangle. But I'm going to call it an <b>Unrequited Oblivious Triangle Wherein No One Expresses Feelings And Everyone Is Somewhat Awful.</b> &lt;--- Much more accurate tbh. You're welcome.<br /><br />See, there is this young Sultan named MEHMED who is actually a little beast but also a winning little battling hellion. He loves Lada. Lada takes a loooooooooooooooooong time to love him back. Radu? RADU IS SO FREAKING IN LOVE WITH MEHMED THAT RADU BASICALLY PACKS HIMSELF OFF SO HE CAN NEVER SEE MEHMED AGAIN. #logic Mehmed has 0% of an idea that Radu loves him so much. Do you see what I mean??? It ain't your average triangle. Considering most of the parties don't even realise the other parties have feelings.<br /><br />And tbh, who has <i>real</i> feelings around here???? They're all so insane and stabby. (Except for Radu who is only 16% stabby and the rest of the time he's charming people and manipulating and spying. GO RADU. But I digress.)<br /><br /><b> • It's 500 pages.</b><br />That, in itself, tells you a lot. <b>AKA = it's tooooo loooooooong.</b> Like I said, there is a TEAPOT LOAD of just explanations about political things. Like, I don't even know, mate, I was so bored. Then there are scenes of wars and battles and running for your life and assassination attempts. <b>There is, obviously, impaling</b>. But not as much as I expected. <b>My favourite scenes were the conversations between Mehmed and Lada and Radu.</b> They were such an awesome and complex and dynamic trio. I will squish them. But I honestly wish the book had been <i>half as long</i> and involved MORE ACTION instead of so much <i>telling</i> vs showing. (I want to SEE, not just be told!) <b>Also there were far too many minor characters.</b> I'm talking DOZENS OF 'EM. I don't even know who was who and heaven help me before I can recall any names. There's a grand betrayal at the end and when it happens I'm like "Say who now does what and why?" because I remembered NO ONE.<br /><br /><b>• It's actually not super graphic.</b><br />I thought it might be?? And while sometimes, stylistically, it read like an adult historical fiction....it really kept the murder and mayhem to TELLING you about it rather than showing. I mean, don't get me wrong, we do have scenes where people are impaled. And stabbed. But altogether, I don't think it was really that bloody. (Well, apart from Lada really torturing eveyrone around here, but she didn't kill them. She was a brutal kid.)<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL:</b><br />You know what? I'm going to have fond feelings for this book. It wasn't an easy read. It was gritty and brutal and cruel and it was intense and actually kind of emotional?! I FREAKING LOVED THE CHARACTERS SO VERY MUCH. I will definitely read more books because I want to know what happens! Even though I am rather confused about the details! Huzzah confusion! It is my middle name apparently!<br /><br />Definitely try this one if you like (A) historical fiction, (B) actually <i>brutal</i> characters, (C) stabbing, (D) tragic precious darlings who turn out to be wicked intelligent, and (E) complex worlds.<br /><br /><br /><br />Although, confession, I'm horribly disappointed it's not <i>Vladette the Impaler</i>. I mean, MISSED OPPORTUNITY THERE. Apparently Ladislav is the female version of Vlad. Which is probably more logical than Vladette, but, ya know. #disappointed</span>
  <a data-text-id="8064758407358054060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1712475963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712475963" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712475963?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712475963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13024676100028931523">Ever since I read this particular quote taken from <b>And I Darken</b>, I've been enchanted:<br/><br/><i>“On our wedding night," she said, "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied.”</i><br/><br/>And also that beautiful cover didn't hurt.<br/><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470937808i/19983280.jpg' width='420' height='234' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/><b>A</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13024676100028931523" style="display:none">Ever since I read this particular quote taken from <b>And I Darken</b>, I've been enchanted:<br><br><i>“On our wedding night," she said, "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied.”</i><br><br>And also that beautiful cover didn't hurt.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470937808i/19983280.jpg" width="420" height="234" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br><b>And I Darken</b> starts out with Lada and Radu's childhood; introducing their vicious father and broken mother.<br><br>Can I just say that, for whatever unknown reason, I absolutely loved their mother. I cannot understand why exactly other than that her determination to escape felt so crucial for me.<br><br><i>“I want to go home,” she whispered. “Back to Moldavia. Please let me.”<br>“Beg.”<br>Vasilissa’s tiny frame trembled. Then she dropped to her knees, lowered her head, and took Vlad’s hand in her own. “Please. Please, I beg of you. Let me go home.”<br>Vlad put out his other hand and stroked Vasilissa’s lank, greasy hair. Then he grabbed it, wrenching her head to the side. She cried out, but he pulled tighter, forcing her to stand. He placed his lips against her ear. “You are the weakest creature I have ever known. Crawl back to your hole and hide there. Crawl!” He threw her down, and, sobbing, she crawled from the room.”</i><br><br>I truly felt for Vasilissa. And I don't know if this is terrible to admit (because she's their mother), but I was extremely glad when Vasilissa managed to escape his cruelty.<br><br>In the meanwhile, we skip a few years to learn the complications set in Radu and Lada's relationship.<br><br><i>“He was so tired and so scared, and she had saved him. “Thank you.” He stumbled toward her with arms outstretched. When he was hurting, his nurse folded him into herself, sealing him away from the world. He wanted—needed—that now.<br>Lada hit him in the stomach. He doubled over in pain, sinking to his knees. She knelt next to him, grasping him by the ears. “Do not thank me. All I did was teach them to fear me. How does that help you? Next time you hit first, you hit harder, you make certain that your name means fear and pain. I will not be here to save you again.”</i><br><br>We slowly learn that Lada does care deeply for her brother, though, in a very particular way i.e scares him away and mocks him, but deep down couldn’t bear to leave him in harm's way.<br><br><i>“When she thought he was sleeping, she crept into his room. Radu did not sleep much, always awake and worrying over something. But he lay as still as possible, keeping his breathing even, curious as to what she would do.<br>She sat beside his bed for a long while. Finally, she put a hand on his shoulder and whispered, “You are mine.”<br>Radu had been thinking about the way Lada sounded when she told him that Costin had escaped the river. The tone of her voice, the lack of an edge. He was almost certain she had lied. He fell asleep, wrapped in the secure warmth of her next to him and nagged by guilt over how happy the day had made him.<br>Still made him.”</i><br><br>Okay, so this has been on my mind for awhile, but did Costin survive or not? (The answer is crucial for my peace.)<br><br>But circling back to the main storyline, complications arise when their father abandons them to be raised in the Ottoman courts for…their education.<br><br><i>“Radu looked to Lada, trying to put together what he was hearing. Lada understood perfectly well what this man was saying. Their lives were valuable only insofar as their father did what he was told. And instead of just taking Radu, Halil Pasha had known what her father valued the most.<br>All those years working toward her father’s love and approval had led her here.<br>It had made her a prisoner.”</i><br><br>And before we move on, I just wanted to mention that Lada and Radu are such phenomenally fleshed-out characters, I'm still in awe.<br><br>And also, this book mentions periods, which, finally. I think this is only my second fantasy book that mentions this completely natural process that almost everyone goes through but doesn't talk about in books.<br><br><i>“When her nurse had told her she would not have to worry about marriage until her monthly courses started, it had been a comfort. Until the morning Lada awoke covered in blood, in her enemy’s house.”</i><br><br>Yes, this is real, this is me.<br><br>I know I keep going off course in my review, but it was important to mention the above.<br><br>In Edirne, Lada and Radu encounter the son of the devil himself. Mehmed the Second, son of Murad. Lada despises the Ottomans and bides her time, planning her vengeance for the day when she can return to Wallachia and claim her birthright. Radu longs only for a place where he feels safe.<br><br>“How do you do that?”<br>“Do what?”<br>“Make people talk to you. Is it because you are a boy?”<br>Radu knew she envied him his ability to persuade people to trust him. She looked sharp, contrary, and sly. Hers was the face of a fox raiding the livestock. Radu’s was the face of an angel. But it hurt Radu that she thought it was a trick. Did anyone ever truly like him, or was she right? Did his face and tongue merely fool them into thinking they did?”<br><br>“People respond to kindness, Lada. They trust a smile more than a promise that you will leave them choking on their own blood.”<br>Lada snorted. “Yes, but my promise is more sincere than your smiles.”<br>She was right, of course. It had been a lifetime since his smile felt like anything more than a desperate and false ploy. He sniffed, trying to keep the mood light, keep his sister calm. “But no one knows that.”<br>“Someday they will, Radu. Someday they will.”<br><br>But when news arrives that Mehmed's older brothers have died, a twisted turmoil ensues. Mehmed's father gives him the title of sultan under the banner of new peace - with his son being only twelve at the time.<br><br><i>“Mehmed looked up at her with tears in his eyes. “You do not understand. The courts—they will never accept me. I was never supposed to be sultan. They will devour me. I have no allies, no one on my side.”<br>Lada smiled viciously, put on her most mocking voice. “So now you would prove me correct. I thought you had your faith as your greatest strength.”<br>Mehmed’s face hardened. “My faith is my strength.”<br>“Then you have your god on your side. What is a court full of sycophants and rivals against that? Wrap yourself in the armor of your faith. Take your throne.”</i><br><br>He follows Lada's advice and ascends to the throne.<br><br>And so we slowly learn that though Mehmed was sultan, he was not in power. But with the help of Lada and her knowledge on various war tactics, he might just make it out alive on the other side.<br><br><i>"She had to keep them safe from Murad’s wrath. She had to turn Mehmed’s rule to their advantage, but she did not know how.”</i><br><br>We continue to have a few bumps on the road:<br><br>• Assassins were after them.<br>• Lada had killed a man.<br>• They ran to the harem to hide for the night.<br>• In the harem, Huma (Mehmed's mother) instructed Radu and Lada to act as if nothing had changed, but to draw no attention to themselves.<br>• Halil Pasha has his own interpretation of what should and shouldn't happen to Mehmed.<br>• Lada and Radu betraying Mehmed in order to keep him and his future as sultan safe.<br><br>We then have a two-year time jump to Amasya:<br><br>Lada, Radu, and Mehmed are a little more grown up and comfortable in their skin.<br><br><i>“Without Radu, she would have gone mad living here. In the two years since they left Edirne, some of the distance between them had closed. They shared blood and secrets enough to know that without each other, they had no one.<br>It was something.<br>Mehmed was the third part of their bond. He considered them his truest friends and only allies. The guilt of knowing better made Lada softer, broke down the anger she had kept up for so long.<br>They were safe here. That was also something.”</i><br><br>And a lot of other intense things happened during their adolescence, I mean I'm still trying to come to terms with all that what went down.<br><br>But the one that my heart enjoyed the most was: Mehmed and Lada.<br><br>When they met up at their secret place, I was overjoyed.<br><br><i>“Did you miss me?” he teased.<br>Sincerity betrayed her, tumbling out of her mouth in a whisper before she could rein it in. “I did.”<br>He put his hands on her waist, as he had done so many times last summer, pulling her under, pushing her, playing. But this time he left his hands there. They were warm through the thin material of her underclothes. His voice was husky, lower than it had been. “I missed you, too.”</i><br><br>Damn you, butterflies.<br><br><i>“He pulled her closer, and Lada warred within herself. Her inclination was to push him away, to cut him with a clever, sharp remark, to find something, anything to do with her hands, her worthless hands that floated uselessly at her sides.<br>Huma’s words echoed in her head. Set him free. Did she truly hold him that way?<br>Did she want to?<br>As though heeding her desperation but heedless of the confusion and fear ringing through her like the clash of blades, her hands lifted and grabbed the back of Mehmed’s head, tangling in his wet hair. And then her lips, from which nothing but poison had ever dropped, found his and were baptized with sweet fire, reborn into something new and wild. His mouth answered hers, lips parting, his teeth catching hers, her tongue meeting his.<br>It felt like fighting.<br>It felt like falling.<br>It felt like dying.<br>“Mehmed?” Radu called, his voice muffled and indistinct, as if Lada’s head were still underwater. She and Mehmed paused their mouth-to-mouth combat, and Lada realized her legs were wrapped around his waist, his hands around the backs of her thighs, their chests pressed together.”</i><br><br>I was really hesitant at first about their romance, but I would be lying if I said that they didn't make me swoon.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470937808ra/19983281.gif" width="270" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But it did feel really painful when we switched POVs to see Radu find out that the person he valued most in the world didn't feel the same.<br><br><i>"He wanted Mehmed to look at him the way he had looked at Lada.<br>He wanted Mehmed to kiss him the way he had kissed Lada.<br>He wanted to be Lada.<br>No, he did not. He wanted to be himself, and he wanted Mehmed to love him for being himself. His question, the question of Mehmed, was finally answered, piercing him and leaving him shaking, silent, on the floor.<br>He did not want this answer.”</i><br><br>Lada and Radu break off after this incident, and many others that occurred over the years... betrayal, defeat, bitterness. And it was damn hard to read.<br>They have saved each other so many times when no one else would, and it was heartbreaking to see them fall apart from one another.<br><br>And then also Lada and Mehmed's honeymoon stage turns a little sour.<br><br><i>“You are staying here!”<br>Lada peeled off his hand and took a step back. “Why?”<br>He was suddenly fascinated by the bruised flowers in his hand. “I need to leave someone I trust in charge of the city.”<br>“Anyone can do that! Nothing of value will be left here!”<br>Mehmed’s gaze was heavy when it finally found her. “Nothing of value?”<br>Understanding hit Lada. She ripped the flowers from his hand and threw them to the ground. “I will not stay behind to watch your brat! I am no nursemaid!”<br>Mehmed blinked rapidly, then shook his head. “Lada, I was not talking about my son. Do you think he is the only thing here I value?”<br>“Then what?”<br>“You! I will not take you into battle! You have no idea what the conditions are like, no idea how many ways there are to die.”<br>“I can handle myself.”<br>“But what about me? What would I do if something happened to you? I have to keep you safe!”<br>She pushed his chest, sending him stumbling, vase shards crunching beneath his boots. “I am not something to be kept!”</i><br><br>I <b>loved</b> this scene because it reminded me of:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470937808ra/19983282.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470937808ra/19983283.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That last line is so damn empowering.<br><br>Mehmed leaves Lada for the following months, keeping her furious and, though she won't admit it, in despair. So when she receives a letter with Radu's signature saying that Mehmed has fallen ill, she is ready to leave everyone behind.<br><br>Until...<br><br><i>“And where is the devil to take me?”<br>Lada whirled around, heart racing. Mehmed leaned in the doorway, mirth twisting the new form the siege had carved his weary face into. He looked haggard, his cheeks stubbled, dark circles beneath his eyes showing weeks of poor sleep. He crossed the room to her, arms open.<br>“You died!” She pushed him away, staring at his face. He was changed, but it was him. Alive. Healthy.<br>“Did I? That is disappointing. I was very much looking forward to being alive for our reunion. Though I feared you would kill me.”</i><br><br>Damn, was I reliefed when he showed up.<br><br>And I knew without a doubt that Lazar had sent that dreaded letter - for reasons I did not yet understand.<br><br>Until I did... and damn, I did not see that ending coming. Everything that happened with Lada, Mehmed, and Radu left me feeling both conflicted and proud. How they had all grown.<br><br><i>“Well, are you ready, Lada Dragwlya, daughter of the dragon?”<br>Fire burned in her heart, and her wounded soul spread out, casting a shadow like wings across her country. This was hers. Not because of her father. Not because of Mehmed. Because the land itself had claimed her as its own.<br>“Not Dragwlya,” she said. “Lada Dracul. I am no longer the daughter of the dragon.” She lifted her chin, sights set on the horizon. “I am the dragon.”</i><br><br>I need to know what will happen to this trio because Kiersten White sure knows how to keep me on edge.<br><br>I'm only certain of two things for the next book:<br><br>It would hurt, and I would need to be strong.<br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>And I Darken</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0553522310/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0553522310&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=e252cd049903952a8e28ee0ccb5d997e" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482930097i/21562738.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482930097i/21562739.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Support creators you love.
