<div id="review_1453221323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453221323" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1453221323?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453221323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8699280302614954757">Ever heard of Vlad the Impaler? He had a reputation for cruelty throughout Europe. He took pleasure in torturing and killing his enemies with his most preferred method being impalement. He was also the inspiration for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula' title='Dracula by Bram Stoker' rel='nofollow noopener'> Dracula</a>. Imagine an alternate history with Vlad the Impaler as a girl. This is our story.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conquerors_Saga__1_' title='And I Darken (The Conquerors Saga #1) by Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'> And I Darken</a> follows Lada’s life from the very beginning. We start in 1435 Transylvania with Vlad Dracul taking in the fact that his wife has given birth to a girl. Such a disgrace because sh</span>
  <span id="freeText8699280302614954757" style="display:none">Ever heard of Vlad the Impaler? He had a reputation for cruelty throughout Europe. He took pleasure in torturing and killing his enemies with his most preferred method being impalement. He was also the inspiration for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula" title="Dracula by Bram Stoker" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dracula</a>. Imagine an alternate history with Vlad the Impaler as a girl. This is our story.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conquerors_Saga__1_" title="And I Darken (The Conquerors Saga #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener"> And I Darken</a> follows Lada’s life from the very beginning. We start in 1435 Transylvania with Vlad Dracul taking in the fact that his wife has given birth to a girl. Such a disgrace because she cannot be an heir. A girl is of no worth unless you marry her off. A year later her brother Radu is born. We follow Lada through other’s eyes in the first few chapters until the book jumps to 1446. From here on forward..the book is set in the dual perspectives of Lada and Radu. It’s pretty straight forward.<br /><br />Lada wants so badly to impress her father Vlad. She wants to prove that even though she is a female, she can be as badass and brutal as the rest of them. In fact, she can be <b>more</b> fierce, dangerous, cruel, strong, etc. than any boy. She’s constantly trying to prove her worth to her father. Even after he uses his children as pawns in a treaty sending them off to be raised in the Ottoman Empire bargaining with their lives.<br /><br />Radu is pretty much the opposite of his sister - not what Vlad would want out of a son. He’s sensitive, emotional, delicate, but so so beautiful. He is constantly seeking Lada’s love and approval. Lada views him as weak, while she is the strong one. She has this hate for her brother, but also an undeniable love. Lada is torn with her feelings on Radu because she constantly needs to protect him yet can’t stand that he can’t do it himself. She envies him for being born with a penis, thus naturally having more power than she could ever possibly have. Lada and Radu's sibling relationship is incredibly complex. It is one of my favorite aspects of the novel. I am very curious to see how it plays out in the future.<br /><br />One of the best things about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conquerors_Saga__1_" title="And I Darken (The Conquerors Saga #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener"> And I Darken</a> is how the themes of politics, religion, and sexuality are all weaved in throughout the plot. I enjoyed how these played such a large part in not only our story, but the characters. There was such a great deal of character development. Politics do play a much larger role in the story than I was originally expecting, but I think I should re-evaluate those expectations. I mean..this is a story telling an alternate history to a man who lived this sort of life..he and his brother were used as political bargaining chips and held in “captivity.” The traumatic experiences built up eventually leading to his ruling of Wallachia as a sadistic leader. How can you tell this story without all the intricate details that led to such an outcome? I am oh so excited to see how Lada continues to become a Vlad the Impaler that we recognize.<br /><br />The story is completely original and unlike anything I’ve ever read. The writing is dark and brutal. The setting is beautifully written and historically accurate. I fell in love with the characters and their individual stories. For the first in a series, this was set up so well. My main fault is the story got slow for a good portion of the book. It started off fantastic and picked up at the end. There is a time when Lada and Radu are caught up in the whole Mehmed thing. I understand why it all went the way it did. I just wish it wasn’t slow for such a large portion of the story. Though I realize this allowed time for character and story development.<br /><br />I am very excited to see how things play out for Lada, Radu, Mehmed, and Wallachia in the sequel. I’m curious how close to history <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3027554.Kiersten_White" title="Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener"> Kiersten White</a> plans on keeping <i>The Conquerors Saga</i>. If you like YA books that tell an alternate history and prefer your books on the darker side, I highly recommend you read this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8699280302614954757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1682540019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1682540019" />
    <a title="lily ☁️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10148904-lily"><img alt="lily ☁️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517405104p2/10148904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1682540019?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lily ☁️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lily ☁️" href="/user/show/10148904-lily">lily ☁️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27153280-and-i-darken">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=tolino">tolino</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1682540019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12867912127432324785">To résumé my experience with this book in seven words: <b>it put me in a reading slump.</b> I really wanted (and expected) to love it, but, oh well.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <u>Here’s a list of all the things I did not do:</u>
</blockquote><br/>・<b>Care about the historical context</b> of this book, which, apparently, is also immensely insulting to the people whose history is being “reimagined”—and while I’m not one of them, the reasoning behind their outrage resonates with me all too well.<br/><br/>・<b>Found the storyline intriguing</b>. Excepting the first 30% of this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText12867912127432324785" style="display:none">To résumé my experience with this book in seven words: <b>it put me in a reading slump.</b> I really wanted (and expected) to love it, but, oh well.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <u>Here’s a list of all the things I did not do:</u>
</blockquote><br />・<b>Care about the historical context</b> of this book, which, apparently, is also immensely insulting to the people whose history is being “reimagined”—and while I’m not one of them, the reasoning behind their outrage resonates with me all too well.<br /><br />・<b>Found the storyline intriguing</b>. Excepting the first 30% of this book, I couldn’t possibly have cared less about what was happening, and to whom, probably because I ceased to<br /><br />・<b>Remain emotionally invested in the characters</b>. I <i>loved</i> Radu, and also appreciated Lada for who she was, right away, but somewhere along their coming of age they became two-dimensional characters at best, as they spent most of their time fawning over a love interest. Obviously, I did not<br /><br />・<b> Care for the romantic aspect</b>. There was so much swooning over Mehmed (who, incidentally, doesn’t have much of a personality). Mehmed, Mehmed, Mehmed. That’s <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lada and Radu <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>’s thought process for what feels like the majority of this book.<br /><br />I was actually quite taken with <i>And I Darken</i> initially, but I slowly found myself bored (I read it in five days, but it actually sat untouched on my current-reads pile for three of those days), unaffected by its contents, and oftentimes annoyed.<br /><br />The only saving grace (hence my rating) in this book is the writing.<br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_1786835244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1786835244?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gorgeous-writing">gorgeous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-friendships">favorite-friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1786835244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7071051782823334335">Listen. Listen. I adore this series. I love it in my soul. Buuuuuut this is a great example of a series where book one is a great setup but <b>book two is where the payoff is</b>. Even though I had some issues here, it should be noted that book two, Now I Rise, is one of my all-time favorite books, <b>improving on every one of my issues with this book.</b>. Top five-single-books-ever level. Feel free to drop on over to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792130445?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a>. <br/><br/>I admit that I loved this slightly more while reading it - I think time and medi</span>
  <span id="freeText7071051782823334335" style="display:none">Listen. Listen. I adore this series. I love it in my soul. Buuuuuut this is a great example of a series where book one is a great setup but <b>book two is where the payoff is</b>. Even though I had some issues here, it should be noted that book two, Now I Rise, is one of my all-time favorite books, <b>improving on every one of my issues with this book.</b>. Top five-single-books-ever level. Feel free to drop on over to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792130445?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a>. <br /><br />I admit that I loved this slightly more while reading it - I think time and meditation has somewhat dulled my opinion. <br /><br /><b>THE BEST BITS</b><br /><br />♔ The worldbuilding is just beautiful. <i>And I Darken</i> is historical fiction, but it's not like historical fiction that you've read before. Honestly, it reads like excellent fantasy. It's cool that history classes about the Ottoman Empire can spoil you about a book. There's some awesome political intrigue in this one, which I REALLY loved. <blockquote>
  <i>"You see this...as a prison. But you are wrong. This is my court. This is my throne. This is my kingdom. The cost was my freedom and my body...So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?"</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />♚ The tension was so palpable. I genuinely felt that these characters could die at any moment. <b>Dramatic tension never faded</b>, and the book is incredibly suspenseful. Yes, there are moments where the plot is slow and the book got boring, but for a 500-page book, this was incredibly engaging. <i>And I Darken</i> truly is very dark, as promised. There is nothing light and fluffy about this book.<br /><br />♔ I liked that White managed to have a misogynistic, borderline-Islamophobic main character, yet not portray either of those messages as positive. Neither of these traits are romanticized by the narrative. In fact, some of the major characters practice Islam, including Radu and later Nazira, and for them it is a consistent positive. I HAVE seen a few ownvoices reviewers mention they felt otherwise about the rep, so I'd check out some other reviews. <br /><br />♚ The writing style of this blew me away. It's so engaging, and gorgeous in a very understated way. So kudos for achieving that balance! <br /><br /><b>MY MIXED FEELINGS ON THE CHARACTER WORK</b><br /><br />Now, here's my real complaint. Lada, Radu, and Mehmed are... <i>sort of</i> well developed... but none of them are all that sympathetic, and they fall into archetypes more than I'd like. <br /><br />♔ Lada is definitely a morally ambiguous and badass character. She's purposefully written as both hatable and sympathetic. She believes she's not like other girls and there's a religious taint to her dislike for the Ottoman Empire. Her dislikability is honestly one of the reasons I am so impressed with her character. Because I should hate her, but somehow, she's my favorite; she's just got a sympathetic edge to her. I did have a few issues, though. First of all, she's not in touch with her emotions unless that emotion is anger, which is fine, but I almost wanted her to have a true breakdown and show the cracks in her armor. That's just my preference in characters coming through, I think. <br /><br />The real issue is that she gets too distracted by Mehmed. <b>Badass female character... until Hot Dude Appears.</b> You know, creativity. To be fair, she keeps her badassery and characterization, even when the book gets too romantic for my taste; it's just frustrating. <br /><br />♚ Radu is an interesting character in the abstract, but <b>his storyline really annoyed me.</b> His main job in this book is to be in love with Mehmed. Unrequited gay love. You know, creativity. This narrative does definitely improve in book two (one of the many things I loved about book two #IworshipNowIRise2k17) but for this book, I'll just say that it really didn't deserve the representation praise. <br /><br />♔ While Mehmed is extremely likeable in the first half, in the second half I kind of hated him. He comes off as <b>a misogynistic ass</b> in some sections. Granted, this was purposeful, but I really just feel like he needs to get off Lada's case.<br /><br />♚ <b>Complex sibling relationships</b> (or rivalries) are the absolute greatest. Radu and Lada's sibling rivalry and contradicting close bond is an absolute triumph. Unfortunately, I wasn't a fan of their dynamic's relationship to <b>that stupid love triangle.</b> In general, there's too much romance; Lada and Mehmed's chemistry was completely nonexistent. Frankly, Mehmed had more chemistry with Radu, but was also portrayed entirely as heterosexual. Again, that unrequited love thing got old FAST. This love triangle is a super creative idea, and I really love it in the abstract, but it got old fast when I realized White had no intentions of portraying Mehmed as anything but straight. <br /><br />All in all, the character work here wasn't bad by any means, but it wasn't quite as engaging for me as so many others have said it was.<br /><br /><b>So, do I recommend this book? Yes, with every bit of my heart.</b> This book was solid already, and then I read an arc of the sequel and it's maybe one of my favorite books of all time. This series owns my ass. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7071051782823334335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2428298828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2428298828" />
    <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis"><img alt="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585764390p2/6603759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2428298828?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis">☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2428298828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1562197297708420318"><b>Why, oh why, oh why, OH FUCKING WHY do English-speaking authors insist on using Slavic names, which they obviously keep fucking misusing????? Can anyoone please explain to me in a layman's terms what so chic or risque can there be about using names you don't know how to use? Have the editors gone extinct? Is there some grand conspiracy to keep me properly irritated?</b> Why the blazing fads can they not get into their obviously thicker than average heads that a boy would be called Vladislav, Alexand</span>
  <span id="freeText1562197297708420318" style="display:none"><b>Why, oh why, oh why, OH FUCKING WHY do English-speaking authors insist on using Slavic names, which they obviously keep fucking misusing????? Can anyoone please explain to me in a layman's terms what so chic or risque can there be about using names you don't know how to use? Have the editors gone extinct? Is there some grand conspiracy to keep me properly irritated?</b> Why the blazing fads can they not get into their obviously thicker than average heads that a boy would be called Vladislav, Alexander, Valentin, Svyatoslav, Miloslav, Radmil (if you want to get really fancy with names) ..., while a girl would be called Vladislava, Alexandra, Valentina, Svyatoslava, Miloslava, Radmila ... Do you not understand that it is maddening to read a book, where a girl gets called 'Ladislav', time and again???????? <br /><br />Another thing, if a girl was called in honor of Vladislav, she should have been called for short Vlada not Lada. And the long version would have been much more likely Vladislava than Ladislava. <br />A girl could have been called Ladislava or Lada had she been named to the honor of an ancient pre-Christian Slavic pagan goddess of female beauty and love, Lada! I repeat, the name Lada is not derived from Vlada, it was an extremely old pagan name... Even the root words are different: Lada is from 'lad' and Vlad is from 'vlad'. We are not being graced by the presence of Professor Snape, we do not need to chop word roots!<br /><br />In Slavic languages it's rare to chop a single consonant on the beginning of a name to get it shorter. It's not English, for Cristsakes! In most cases Slavic (as well as many used in Slavic countries names of Greek, Aramaic or Roman origins) names get shortened from the end not from the beginning: Olga becomes Olya, Mariya - Masha, Valentina - Valya, Alevtina - Alya, Glafira - Glafa, Natalya - Nata or Natasha, Lyudmila - Lyuda or (rarer) Mila, Lyubov - Lyuba, Sofiya - Sofa or Sofochka or Sofiushka or even Sophie (with Francais-like accent), Zinaida - Zina (not In(n)a or Ida, those would be different names!), even Serafima would become either Sera or Fima, just like Margarita would become either Rita or Margo (not Garita!). Basically, all 1-letter beginning choppings that I can think of involve: Elizaveta - Liza, Elena - Lena, Anastasiya - Nastya, - and it's always a vowel dropped off, not a consonant. You don't make a Ristina out of Kristina! Klavdiya becomes a Klava not Lavdiya! And Svyatoslava never would become a Vyatoslava! <br /><br />If this feels too difficult why even bother using the oh-so-impossible-to-use-correctly names of Slavic origins? Or why not call by them only male characters? <br /><br /><b>The history?</b> It's taking a walk or maybe a flying leap (from the nearest bridge, it seems) in a bid to get rid of writers in paroxisms of flying fantasy. What's important is it's absent from this book. <b>It has taken a giant vacation from this plot. Farewell.</b> No point in getting offended or not offended or researching Vlad Țepeș or the Ottoman empire or whatever... The names are mostly placeholders. The plot could have happened almost anywhere where women had social issues. Which is almost everywhere. <br /><br /><b>The characters? I don't know why they were supposed to have bothered to live.</b> I don't know how many dymentional they were but most of them definitely were missing personality pieces. For one thing, it's cool to see a girl character strong enough to chew steel (not literally but then... no one gave her this chance...), ramrod straight (both in body and in her wonderfully social skills), calculating, greedy (my Wallachia!!!), supposedly people-loving (even though this never brought any of them any good, from what I read). For another, <b>she was bullying bullies not to bully her brother, simultaneously bullying the said 'weak' brother into outbullying the bullies</b>. <b>It's a mess...</b> An entertaining one. But nevertheless <b>messy</b>. I like strong characters. This is beyond a strong character. <b>This a Terminator in the throes of android rage on parade.</b> (How do you go about attacking 2 soldiers with 1 knife and 1 sidekick?)<br /><br /><b>Why Dracula? Bram Stoker might have bit someone.</b> <br /><br />The book had some cool quotes and the character of our trans<s>vestite</s>named heroine was sort of unusual but I was too irritated to bother. I will add some of those quotes soon, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1562197297708420318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1691843324?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1691843324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14762943628519258847">'And I Darken' was the first book that I've ever read by Ms. Kiersten White, but it certainly won't be the last. The first book in 'The Conquerers' series, it managed to completely captivate me. I am both intrigued, enamored, and at times appalled, by these characters and the turbulent world that they occupy.<br/><br/>Lada Dragwlya is an unlikely heroine. She's unattractive, uncouth and at times, downright mean. She's everything her father had hoped for in a son, but got in his daughter. Her only redeemin</span>
  <span id="freeText14762943628519258847" style="display:none">'And I Darken' was the first book that I've ever read by Ms. Kiersten White, but it certainly won't be the last. The first book in 'The Conquerers' series, it managed to completely captivate me. I am both intrigued, enamored, and at times appalled, by these characters and the turbulent world that they occupy.<br /><br />Lada Dragwlya is an unlikely heroine. She's unattractive, uncouth and at times, downright mean. She's everything her father had hoped for in a son, but got in his daughter. Her only redeeming qualities are her love for her homeland, Wallachia, and her love for her younger brother, Radu.<br /><br />By comparison, Radu is everything that Lada is not. He is soft-spoken and gentle, an utter disappointment to their father, the Prince of Wallachia. Immediately, Radu claimed a piece of my heart.<br /><br />When their father trades Lada and Radu to the Sultan of Ottoman as pawns to guarantee his loyalty, they are left to fend for themselves in a hostile new world. Lada is determined to be strong and to plan for her eventual revenge on the Sultan and his countrymen. She refuses to show any weakness that might be used against her and Radu.<br /><br />Unlike his sister, Radu soon takes to the ways of this new world. He never felt that he fit in in Wallachia and finds comfort in this new country. He is not resistant to the new teachings or the new religion, as Lada is. <br /><br />After months living in the Ottoman Empire, Radu and Lada make an unlikely friend. Mehmed is the illegitimate son of the sultan. Before long, the three are inseparable. The line between friend and enemy blurs and loyalties are called into question.<br /><br />From start to finish, I was completely captivated by this story. It has a little of everything. There's plenty of action and battle scenes. There's romance and angst. Kingdoms rise and are overthrown. The incredible highs are off-set by bitter betrayals. <br /><br />I am completely and totally hooked on this story. It is the first book, in what I'm sue will prove to be an epic saga. The characters were certainly flawed, but that only made me love them more. As soon as the next book is released, I'll be diving in again. I was left with a lot of questions and I'll have to wait for the next book to get my answers.<br /><br />I listened to the Audible version of this book and I thought that the narration was well done. I could easily distinguish between the characters and I thought the narrator did a great job of conveying the emotions and intensity. It was a fantastic audiobook choice for me.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14762943628519258847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2596520885?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553522341" href="/book/show/34001683-and-i-darken">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596520885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer780961010045450202">in the interest of full transparency, this was not what i was expecting. not in the least. and i think its due to the fact this book is labelled as fantasy, which is misleading because there was no fantasy element to this story at all. its straight up historical fiction. this was about two siblings who befriend mehmed (the conquerer) and experience his early years as the sultan of the ottoman empire. <br/><br/>but the more i think about it, the more i actually enjoyed this? which surprises me because worl</span>
  <span id="freeText780961010045450202" style="display:none">in the interest of full transparency, this was not what i was expecting. not in the least. and i think its due to the fact this book is labelled as fantasy, which is misleading because there was no fantasy element to this story at all. its straight up historical fiction. this was about two siblings who befriend mehmed (the conquerer) and experience his early years as the sultan of the ottoman empire. <br /><br />but the more i think about it, the more i actually enjoyed this? which surprises me because world history was my worst subject in school! hehe. <br /><br />this was very heavy when it came to court politics and war strategising, which did not interest me at all. where the story really shined for me was the dynamic between the main characters. i really felt for lada and radus relationship as siblings. as someone who isnt close to their brother, i could really empathise with what they were going through. and seeing how mehmeds friendship with each of them grew and changed things was just so hard to watch, but also really touching. i thought the character depth and development was simply phenomenal. <br /><br />im pretty sure i will continue this series for the characters alone. if i wanted to know more about the expansion of the ottoman empire, i would pick up a text book. but these characters made the story completely worth while. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1722260792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1722260792" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1722260792?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1722260792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7734911069607144832"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>A gem of a book.</b><br/>It was <b>savage</b> and <b>brilliant</b>, a bloody tale of <b>politics</b> laced with <b>tainted relationships, betrayals and desire</b>. For freedom, for power, for human touch. For greatness.<br/><br/>In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_' title='And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'>And I Darken</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3027554.Kiersten_White' title='Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kiersten White</a> travels through time to medieval Wallachia, a vassal state of the blooming Ottoman Empire. To the court of Vlad Dracul, the cruel fat</span>
  <span id="freeText7734911069607144832" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>A gem of a book.</b><br />It was <b>savage</b> and <b>brilliant</b>, a bloody tale of <b>politics</b> laced with <b>tainted relationships, betrayals and desire</b>. For freedom, for power, for human touch. For greatness.<br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3027554.Kiersten_White" title="Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiersten White</a> travels through time to medieval Wallachia, a vassal state of the blooming Ottoman Empire. To the court of Vlad Dracul, the cruel father that terrified his son, and mesmerized his daughter. Until he gave them away to the Sultan in order to secure his reign, and left them among foes ready to devour them. Lada was always ferocious. Refusing to forget her country, despite her traitorous father, determined to set it free from Ottoman rule, from any oppressor. Radu was always tame. Afraid but socially skilled, he could entrance anyone to do his bidding. Their relationship was not an easy one, but it got more complicated when they met and befriended Mehmed, the Sultan's third son. For them he was an ally. Their only ally. For him they were his honest friends, whom he trusted unconditionally. What happens though when love collides with duty? With ambition? With loyalty? And what is the cost of ultimate power?<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I love Wallachia. It belongs to me, and I belong to it. It is my country, and it should always be mine, and I hate any king or sultan or god or prophet that proclaims anyone else has any right to it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />If there is one lesson to be learned from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a>, is that <b>History is a matter of perspective</b>. The hero of a nation is the bane of another. The greatest victory of one army, painted with the most glorious colours, is the most somber memory of the defeated. We are aware of great events that took place centuries before our time, but we fail to wonder about the men behind them, the person behind the leader. Which were his motivations? How passionate was he about his goals? What was the source of them? It was with a heavy heart that I realized halfway through the book that Mehmed was not just a Mehmed. He was <i>the</i> Mehmed. Mehmed II the Conqueror. The man that conquered my country and sentenced it to nearly 400 years of slavery. You can understand why I was at least prejudiced against him. But what astonished me was that throughout the story, even though his character had many weaknesses and I wasn't exactly fond of him, I came to <b>begrudgingly admire</b> his dedication, his cunning and sharp mind and that was the result of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3027554.Kiersten_White" title="Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiersten White</a>'s writing. She was objective. She painted with deadly accuracy the good and the bad, without taking sides. She didn't favour Wallachia or Ottoman Empire. She took events and people who actually existed and walked this earth and infused the dry stories left by historians with <b>life, passion, with tragedies and cruelty</b> that made your body feel like a live wire, humming with energy and tension, desperate to unleash them. Through lush descriptions, luxury to the extent of extravagance, religious quests, customs that may disorientate your moral compass and constant plots, <b>she crafted a world gritty yet foreign</b>. She did not romanticise war and court intrigue. She was an experienced guide to the barracks of the Janisaries, the harems and the mosques, the schemes, the rise and fall of empires, and to the paths Lada, Radu and Mehmed followed. Paths where, as you crossed them, the light was slowly diminishing until you were left alone in the dark.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Her spine was steel. Her heart was armor. Her eyes were fire.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>Lada. Radu. Mehmed.</b><br /><b>A toxic triangle, a poisonous threesome bound by love, lust and yearning</b>. In a way, they broke and reshaped each other. Lada was an extraordinary character. By changing Vlad the Impaler to Lada the Impaler, the author created a mean, ruthless and passionate figure, fixed on finding a place in the wolrd meant only for her, without depending on the graces of a man, whoever that man might be. She was the Daugher of the Dragon. The Daughter of Wallachia. A living and breathing menace, torn between her burning desire to return to her Mother, to liberate her Mother, and her complicated feelings for Radu and Mehmed. While Lada was sharp as steel, Radu was soft and pleasant. He held his sister accountable for many of his misfortunes, he was jealous of her and intimidated at the same time, but he found a way to rise. To use his talents. For Mehmed. The bright star that blinded both siblings. Guided by the belief that he was chosen to do the unthinkable, to conquer Constantinople, he had little regard for the lives that would be lost. The three of them committed terrible crimes. They betrayed each other, and kept facing the same questions, without being able to answer; Is one life worth less than a thousand? Is heartbreak sanctioned in order to protect the ones you love? What is the ultimate sacrifice they would make for the accomplishment of everything they'd ever wanted?<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Souls and thrones are irreconcilable.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a>'s main pillars are politics and power.</b> Having that in mind, you will bear witness to devastating choices, to a plethora of plots and bloodshed of those getting in the way. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3027554.Kiersten_White" title="Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiersten White</a> won't encourage you to pick a side, though. That is your choice and your choice alone. You will wobble, curse, cry out of frustration and then wobble some more. In the end, it doesn't matter what (or whom) you choose. All that matters is that you will feel an odd kinship with these damaged characters. You will experience the clash of religions, of dreams and calls and ambitions. And you will feel yourself darken in the process.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“And so she cut out her heart and offered it as a sacrifice. She would pay whatever price her mother Wallachia demanded.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/658-andidarken" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more over at <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest.eu</a>!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7734911069607144832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692197691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18378270174030994518"><blockquote>
  <i>"It is the way of the world. You can be the aggressor, you can fight against crusaders on their own land, or you can stay at home and wait for them to come to you. And they <i>would</i> come. They would come with fire, with disease, with swords and blood and death. Weakness is an irresistible lure."</i>
</blockquote>4.5 stars.<br/><br/>Lada made an awesome first impression, not everyone can claim to be a badass right from birth. She wasn't exactly relatable - most of the time I couldn't figure out what her motivations were - </span>
  <span id="freeText18378270174030994518" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"It is the way of the world. You can be the aggressor, you can fight against crusaders on their own land, or you can stay at home and wait for them to come to you. And they <i>would</i> come. They would come with fire, with disease, with swords and blood and death. Weakness is an irresistible lure."</i>
</blockquote>4.5 stars.<br /><br />Lada made an awesome first impression, not everyone can claim to be a badass right from birth. She wasn't exactly relatable - most of the time I couldn't figure out what her motivations were - but I couldn't help loving her no matter what. <br /><br />I feel like Radu and Lada switched places in terms of gender and sexuality. Lada never wanted to be female and Radu never acted like a traditional male. Perhaps this came from their lack of adult role models growing up. <br /><br />Mehmed made me angry sometimes... his determination to conquer Constantinople despite how many people would get killed in the process, and especially his obliviousness as the center of a love triangle. Every time he drove a wedge between Lada and Radu I wanted to strangle him, because Lada and Radu are my sibling bromance OTP - my <b>brOTP</b>. They should stand by one another no matter what.<br /><br />The ending was bittersweet. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's great that Lada is taking charge of her life without relying on any man, and I agree that she and Mehmed wouldn't have worked out even if they did get married. But the thought of Radu and Lada so many miles apart, and Radu still pining over Mehmed who will never love him back... *sobs* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Actually, about that: does anyone think it's possible Mehmed is bisexual? Sometimes he seemed to get strangely physical with Radu. Maybe that's just me and my wishful thinking.<br /><br />Will be desperately waiting for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22817331.Untitled__The_Conquerors_Saga__2_" title="Untitled (The Conquerors Saga #2) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Rise</a> until 2017.</span>

    <blockquote>•full review posted now•</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>“On our wedding night," she said, "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I'm in the process of giving my grades up for adoption because I'm unfit to raise them myself. <br><br>Is there any possibility that I can trade my grades for Radu and Lada?? <br><br>Because now, I'd be fucking fabulous at raising them. <br><br><s>this is all lies; they'd probably end up raising me </s><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459939270ra/18674844.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know it’s been like 65 years since I’ve finished this book. I have no excuses besides being the world's biggest procrastinator but hey look at me. I deserve an A++ for managing to type up all of this.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“We cannot always have what we want, no matter how much we want it.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><i>And I Darken</i>, was as beautiful as the cover. I don't know whether it devoured me or I devoured it but the point is.......😍. It actually made my procrastinator self want to walk around in public and telling every human being, <i>"If you don't read this....are you really living?" </i>. Truthfully, I don't know what part in this book I declared I'm officially in love but all you need to know is that...you will love this. Not only because the synopsis will completely enamor you but the characters will make you want to throw up your soul and give it to them in a silver platter. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517729820ra/24999798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>What's this book about??? </u><br><br><b>PLOT </b><br><br>✔️From beginning to end, you're thrown into a world filled with violence, abuse, dark, finding oneself and somewhat loving??<br>✔️ If you read the synopsis, you won't be let down. <br>✔️ Usually, I tend to stay away from giving anything about the plot and that's what I shall do. <br>✔️ <s> honestly i don't even know where to begin like how does one explain this book ?? and actually make sense?? like I don't even understand my own self.</s> <br>✔️ All I will tell you is that; the plot is very unique and interesting.<br>✔️ it's 5000 times better to go in as clueless as possible with zero expectations<br>✔️ You'd appreciate way way WAY more <br>✔️ Plus watching the plot unravel and tie together is the best feeling <br>✔️ I thought I knew what I was signing myself up for<br>✔️ I thought wrong <br>✔️ 😭<br><br><b>CHARACTERS</b><br><br>✔️ I know I know<br>✔️ I'm already a mother of 75875845845 fictional characters but like what is two more?? <br>✔️ that's hardly anything<br>✔️ pfftttt....<br>✔️ listen i dare you to resist Radu and Lada <br>✔️ <b>P.S: </b> i'm not saying <b> you will fail at this </b> but that's exactly what I'm saying<br><br><br>If I were to explain the characters then I rather do it by using gifs. <br><br><b> Meet Lada:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517731358ra/24999842.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Meet Radu</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/541671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is all. <br><br>I rest my case. <br><br>Don't even fight me on this. <br><br><br><b>THE WRITING</b> <br><br>✔️ Whoa there buddy<br>✔️ I might as well become the heart emoji because that was all I ever was from beginning to end<br>✔️ i think you need further clarification <br>✔️ this was me<br>✔️ 😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍😍<br>✔️ In all seriousness, the writing was exquisite and everything was beautifully detailed. I may or may not have drooled but ssh you didn't hear that from me. <br>✔️ It made picking quotes hard because I simply loved everything. <br><br><b> OTHER THINGS I LOVED </b> <br><br>✔️ Guys, It had a lot of history and I'm a fan of history so basically yes yes yes<br>✔️ I can't forget the representation of different sexualities <br>✔️ and y'all will be proud of this because I am <br>✔️ It even includes Islam which still makes me want to scream in joy<br>✔️ EVERYTHING WAS WELL EXECUTED AND I WANT MORE OF THIS <br>✔️ as in....right now. <br><br><b>WHAT I DIDN'T LIKE </b> <br><br>✔️ if you're reading this review then you're probably wondering why I gave it 4.5 stars?<br>✔️ well that's easy to explain <br>✔️ Mehmed<br>✔️ That is all <br>✔️ <s> I should've wrote this review before finishing Book 2 because now i'm lost as to where my opinion of mehmed changed. </s> <br><br><br>I think y'all already know what i'm going to say next but if you didn't then listen up buddy. If you don't pick this book up sometime in your life then I will come to your house and do this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505946277ra/23974194.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To put it kindly, you won't regret picking this book up. Give it a chance and let it surprise you. I hope you enjoy it as much as I did :) <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I cannot afford to lose you, too"<br>"You cannot lose something you do not own. Take me with you” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>********************<br><br><u>pre-review </u><br><br><i>{calls help line} </i><br><br><b>me:</b> i tried to resist it but it gave me that, <i>"i know you want me"</i> look.<br><b>person:</b> ???<br><b>me:</b> and i can't <br><b>me:</b> and i tried<br><b>me:</b> and i failed<br><b>me:</b> this title just fucking suits my mood<br><br>this makes no sense, just like my entire life but the point is <b> i want to read it and understand the hype.</b> This book was all over my feed so it better be goddamn beautiful and make me feel things or else i'll start a riot. <br><br>and i will ;p</span>

<div id="review_1510726580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510726580" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510726580?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=best-reads-of-2016">best-reads-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2016">published-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510726580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer390694572693592947"><b>Dear Kiersten White,</b><br/><br/>Thank you for restoring my faith in the YA Fantasy genre. I’ve had bad luck with it this year and I really needed someone to show me that the genre wasn’t the problem, and I wasn’t the problem, but instead I was just reading the wrong books.<br/><br/>Thank you for making me feel so much. For filling me up to the brim with emotion. Love, hatred, happiness, despair, frustration, glee, anxiety, <i>passion</i>. I felt it all while reading <i>And I Darken</i> and I can’t remember the last time a book did</span>
  <span id="freeText390694572693592947" style="display:none"><b>Dear Kiersten White,</b><br /><br />Thank you for restoring my faith in the YA Fantasy genre. I’ve had bad luck with it this year and I really needed someone to show me that the genre wasn’t the problem, and I wasn’t the problem, but instead I was just reading the wrong books.<br /><br />Thank you for making me feel so much. For filling me up to the brim with emotion. Love, hatred, happiness, despair, frustration, glee, anxiety, <i>passion</i>. I felt it all while reading <i>And I Darken</i> and I can’t remember the last time a book did this to me. <br /><br />Thank you for writing about a setting and time period that I’ve never seen before and thus gave this book an air of originality and doing it so excellently.<br /><br />Thank you for not shying away from making your book all about politics. Thank you for making those political aspects easily accessible to anyone regardless of prior knowledge or reading experience, without ever trivializing it. <br /><br />Thank you for all the fleshed-out, authentic characters, but most of all Lada. Thank you for Lada. Just that. <br /><br />Thank you for the ending, which was exactly what I wanted to happen throughout the entire second half of the book, but wasn’t sure would. <br /><br />Thank you for slowly killing me from the inside in the best possible way. You’ve probably put me in a book hangover for the rest of the year.<br /><br /><b>Thank you for giving me everything I never knew I wanted.</b><br /><br />Sincerely,<br />Chantal<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I cannot afford to lose you, too"<br />"You cannot lose something you do not own. Take me with you”</i>
</blockquote><br />It’s perhaps important for me to note that this book cannot strictly be considered “Fantasy”. There is no magic and it doesn’t even take place in a different world from our own. Instead, <b>it’s an alternate history retelling, set in Eastern Europe during the reign of the Ottoman Empire.</b> It is based on history, but not historically accurate. I say this, because if you go into it expecting a fast-paced, magic-filled world, you will be disappointed. It reads more like a YA historical fiction, than fantasy. <b>Kiersten White took a real historical figure, Vlad the Impaler, Prince of Wallachia, and turned history on its head.</b> What if this man, who has a reputation for cruelty and found pleasure in torturing and killing, was a girl? <b>The premise is intriguing to say the least, but a lot could have gone wrong and I’m happy to say it didn’t.</b><br /><br />The plot, which could easily have been boring and repetitive, was exciting and didn’t ever bore me. Not once. <b>I was hooked from the first chapter and couldn’t put the book down, even if at times, I needed to take a break just to give my poor heart some time to deal with all the feelings.</b> I love intricate political back-and-forths and character-driven stories and this book did both wonderfully. Kiersten White knows exactly how to create tension, when to resolve misunderstandings right before they become frustrating, when to switch POV and how to make a rather slow book not feel slow-paced.<br /><br />How can I talk about the characters without melting into a little puddle of mush? <b>In short, this cast of characters was one of the best I’ve ever come across.</b> They were both great standing on their own, as well as their dynamics with others. <b>All of them were fleshed-out and three-dimensional, thoroughly flawed yet lovable and at times so relatable it hurt.</b> I went into the book expecting to like Lada (and she did turn out to be my favourite) but I also loved the other characters. Sweet Radu with his good but emotionally scarred soul, Mehmed who does so much wrong and I sometimes wanted to slap but I warmed to anyways, Nikolai who is just the best, and all the female characters of the court who taught Lada what it means to be a woman in their world and how to be powerful and that the two aren’t irreconcilable.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Ugh," she muttered, tugging his hair. "You are so pretty. Like a delicate butterfly beneath my boot."<br />"Ugh, " he replied, pulling one of her own curls, which were thick and coarse. "You are so mad. Like a rabid hound that needs to be put down.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>The relationship between the two siblings was one of my favourite aspects of the novel.</b> Their dynamics were done with such realism and honesty that it had me in awe. That wavering between affection, resentment and jealousy felt palpable and in many ways, their relationship was the driving force of the novel. <br /><br /><b>Lada herself was wonderful and one of my new favourite female characters.</b> She is so fierce, so brutal, at times evil, but somehow she’s also incredibly relatable, something I did not expect. She’s a badass for sure but so much more than that. <b>Her intelligence and calculating nature fascinated me and all I wanted was for her to be happy, to give her a hug and be her best friend.</b> Lada blows other anti-heroines, like Adelina from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_" title="The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Young Elites</a>, out of the water. She’s also a YA main character who isn’t pretty and yields that knowledge like a blade. <b>Watching her fury unfold and seeing the fear, thirst and <i>want</i> behind it was utterly captivating.</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The last time she was up here, she had been... staring up at the sky and dreaming of stars. Now, she looked down and plotted flames.</i>
</blockquote><br />The dynamics between the characters were fabulous to read, though not always a pleasure. <b>There is so much in this book: romance, friendship, sibling love and rivalry; it’s about power struggles and loyalty and the meaning of family.</b> Feminism was clearly an important element but wasn’t ever over-the-top or lecturing and I don’t think I’ve ever read a book that treated power and its importance (both on a personal and macro level) quite so well. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“So the question becomes, Daughter of the Dragon, what will you sacrifice? What will you let be taken away so that you, too, can have power?”</i>
</blockquote><br />I applaud the author for her elaboration on religion and her respectful way of talking about Islam, Christianity and Atheism. The novel also contains <b>unrequited love</b> (and lots of it) a topic that I always want to see, but that I’ve found to be astonishingly sparse in YA literature. <br /><br /><b>The fact that the author managed to interweave all of this seamlessly, still has me in awe. The sheer relatability I felt while reading this whole book was amazing: I felt like I knew these characters and seeing them struggle with so many things that I struggle with daily (though on a completely different scope), made me feel understood and less lonely with my feelings.</b><br /><br />Kiersten White’s writing was beautiful and a huge departure from her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7719245.Paranormalcy__Paranormalcy___1_" title="Paranormalcy (Paranormalcy, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Paranormalcy</a> series I read from her years ago. Quietly poetic without being purple and always effective and poignant.<br /><br />To give you an idea of what to expect, I would probably compare <i>And I Darken</i> most closely to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235.The_Winner_s_Kiss__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___3_" title="The Winner's Kiss (The Winner's Trilogy, #3) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a> by Marie Rutkoski (also two of my favourites). If you loved that trilogy, I’m pretty sure you will love this one too. Otherwise, I know this book isn’t for everyone, as I can see people finding it dragging and slow-paced, but for me it worked perfectly and I full-heartedly recommend it. <br /><br />I’m going to stop gushing now, just know this: <b>I loved everything about this book and it will end up on my list of favourites for 2016 for sure.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="390694572693592947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616844460" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9370392583011210311">When I saw the premise for this story..A female anti-hero retelling of Vlad the Impaler..in a sort of Game of Thorns vibe..I was all set to start handing out some stars.<br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919438.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The book starts with Lada (Ladislav-but she will punch you in the face for calling her that) and her brother Radu growing up in Wallachia. Lada wants to impress her father Vlad so that she can prove that even though born female she is a force to be reckoned with. And she is..<br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919439.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/> <b>Occasionally she informed her tutors when a to</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9370392583011210311" style="display:none">When I saw the premise for this story..A female anti-hero retelling of Vlad the Impaler..in a sort of Game of Thorns vibe..I was all set to start handing out some stars.<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919438.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The book starts with Lada (Ladislav-but she will punch you in the face for calling her that) and her brother Radu growing up in Wallachia. Lada wants to impress her father Vlad so that she can prove that even though born female she is a force to be reckoned with. And she is..<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919439.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> <b>Occasionally she informed her tutors when a torture method appeared to be less effective than others. They ground their teeth and whispered that she had no soul.</b><br><br>Her brother is the complete opposite of Lada, Radu is handsome and meek. Sensitive to a fault. He gets beat up a ton except for the times that Lada uses her fists to get him out of a jam. She tells him that no one will kill him but her. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461851575i/18919440._SY540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Their father Vlad is a spineless turd and he puts the kids off on the Ottoman empire. Their lives are at stake if he does not keep his treaty bargains. Lada HATES it there. They later try to marry her off and that works out just great...<br><b>Lada spoke with a quiet, clear voice, and the room hushed in surprise. No one expected a gril to speak. she was probably not allowed to. Radu knew Lada would not care either way. "On our wedding night," she said, "I will cut out your tongue and swallow it. Then both tongues that spoke our marriage vows will belong to me, and I will be wed only to myself. You will most likely choke to death on your own blood, which will be unfortunate, but I will be both husband and wife and therefore not a widow to be pitied."</b><br><br>That really works out well...then the Sultan's son Mehmed meets Lada and Radu and wants to be their friends.<br> <b>Lada huffed, exasperated. "Very well. What exactly does a friend do?"<br>"I have never had one. I was hoping you would know."<br>"Then you are even more stupid than you look. Radu is the one who makes friends. I am the one who makes people want to whip me."</b><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919441.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>See what an awesome character that Lada is?<br>The first part of this book had me all fangirly and then around 50% I started to lose interest. Mehmed started to get on my nerves..I mean grinding hard on my nerves.<br><br>Both Lada and Radu were both all in lust/love/some shit with him. I really thought he knew of both their feelings and played it to his advantage. Radu is the one who had true feelings for the idiot and he saw Lada and Mehmed all smooching and it crushed him. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919442.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Bleck. The politics kind of took over the story and I'm sorry but that stuff was boring and went on way too long. This book is a chunker and it felt like words were just getting added and repeated over and over again.<br> Mehmed's character just wasn't strong enough for me to want him to be Sultan. I kept hoping that either Lada would come to her senses or some assassin would finally really act like Game of Thrones on his stupid ass. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461851575ra/18919443.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm going with 2.5 stars rounded up to three..just because I want to have hope for Lada's character.<br><br><i>Booksource: Netgalley in exchange for review.</i><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461851575i/18919444._SX540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>My friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617279926?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Hershey</a> and I kinda had an unofficial buddy read with this book. Her review for it is freaking awesome.<br><br><br><br></span>
